  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_77347240-3a9a-4e9b-9014-14003a345555'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer6293508769101958699">Created by Kenturo Miura, Berserk is manga mayhem to the extreme - violent, horrifying, and mercilessly funny - and the wellspring for the internationally popular anime series. Bearer of a gigantic </span>
  <span id="freeText6293508769101958699" style="display:none">Created by Kenturo Miura, Berserk is manga mayhem to the extreme - violent, horrifying, and mercilessly funny - and the wellspring for the internationally popular anime series. Not for the squeamish or the easily offended, Berserk asks for no quarter - and offers none! <br /><br />His name is Guts, the Black Swordsman, a feared warrior spoken of only in whispers. Bearer of a gigantic sword, an iron hand, and the scars of countless battles and tortures, his flesh is also indelibly marked with The Brand, an unholy symbol that draws the forces of darkness to him and dooms him as their sacrifice. But Guts won't take his fate lying down; he'll cut a crimson swath of carnage through the ranks of the damned - and anyone else foolish enough to oppose him! Accompanied by Puck the Elf, more an annoyance than a companion, Guts relentlessly follows a dark, bloodstained path that leads only to death...or vengeance.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10773845805089067311">Berserk, Vol. 1 of 37 (Berserk #1), Kentaro Miura<br/><br/>The philosophical battle between Guts (the Black Swordsman) and Griffith (White Hawk), freedom vs. tranquility. <br/><br/>The story centers on the characters of Guts, a lone mercenary, and Griffith, the leader of a mercenary band called the "Band of the Hawk". Themes of isolation, camaraderie, and the question of whether humanity is fundamentally good or evil pervade the story, as it explores both the best and worst of human nature. Both the manga and anime</span>
  <span id="freeText10773845805089067311" style="display:none">Berserk, Vol. 1 of 37 (Berserk #1), Kentaro Miura<br /><br />The philosophical battle between Guts (the Black Swordsman) and Griffith (White Hawk), freedom vs. tranquility. <br /><br />The story centers on the characters of Guts, a lone mercenary, and Griffith, the leader of a mercenary band called the "Band of the Hawk". Themes of isolation, camaraderie, and the question of whether humanity is fundamentally good or evil pervade the story, as it explores both the best and worst of human nature. Both the manga and anime are noted for their use of graphic violence and sexual content.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز هجدهم ماه جولای سال 2016 میلادی<br /><br />برزرک یک مجموعه مانگا ژاپنی است که توسط «کنتارو میورا» نوشته و طراحی شده‌ است. داستان برزرک در سده های میانی میلادی و در یک دنیای خیالی حول محور شخصیت گاتس، یک مزدور یتیم و گریفیث رهبر گروهی از مزدوران که به «گروه شاهین» معروف بودند، رخ می‌دهد. کنتارو میورا برای نخستین بار نسخه ی اولیه «برزرک» را در سال ۱۹۸۸ میلادی در ۴۸ صفحه به نمایش گذاشت، و برنده ی جایزه مدرسه کومی مانگا گشت، که در آنجا ثبت نام کرده بود. نخستین جلد از مانگا در روز ۲۶ ماه نوامبر سال ۱۹۹۰ میلادی توسط هاکوسنشا در جتز کامیک منتشر می‌شد. در سال ۱۹۹۲م پس از انتشار سه جلد نخستین، انتشار «برزرک» در مجله یانگ انیمال تاکنون ادامه پیدا کرده‌ است. مانگا و انیمه مجموعه برزرک به خاطر استفاده فراوان از خشونت و محتوای جنسی شهرت دارد<br /><br />یک جنگجوی اسرارآمیز که خود را با نام شمشیرزن سیاه معرفی می‌کند، به دنبال پادشاه کشوری به نام سرزمین میانه است.هنگام مبارزه با پیروان پادشاه با دیدن درد و خونریزی، ذهن این جنگجو به زمان گذشته و مسیری که طی کرده بود تا به وضعیت حال خویش برسد برگشت.دریکی از روزها یک گروه ولگرد در حال آزار دختری جوان بودند که به یکباره مورد حمله قرار گرفتند.شمشیرزن سیاه بازگشته بود. او شمشیری بزرگ به اندازه کینه خود دربرابر پادشاه با خود حمل می‌نمود.درحالی که به تنهایی در جنگل به سر می‌برد، شمشیرزن سیاه به سال‌های گذشته و دورانی که در گروهی به نام گروه شاهین به سر می‌برد بازگشت، گروهی متشکل از مزدوران به رهبری شخصی زیبرو و باجذبه به نام گریفیث که آرزو داشت روزی به یک شاه تبدیل شود.گاتس بواسطهٔ نفرین شیطانی که بر روی گردنش حک شده، به عنوان شمشیرزنی سیاهپوش دنبال حواریونی است که او را به سوی خود فرا می‌خوانند. این نشانی است که بر روی قسمتی از بدن قربانیان تقدیم شده به تاریکی زده می‌شود و بدین سبب هنگامی که نور خورشید و روشنایی وجود ندارد باعث جذب ارواحی که قصد تسخیر جسم او را دارند می‌شود.در برابر هیولاهای کوچک این نشان کمی تحریک شده که همراه با سوزش و خون آمدن از آن است، اما هرقدر که شیطان قدرتمندتر باشد باعث تحریک‌پذیری بیشتری نیز می‌باشد و این موضوع تا حد مرگ نیز ادامه دارد. ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_1067131857" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1067131857" />
    <a title="ΕιζΝιnΕ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4483727-n"><img alt="ΕιζΝιnΕ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597836400p2/4483727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1067131857?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ΕιζΝιnΕ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ΕιζΝιnΕ" href="/user/show/4483727-n">ΕιζΝιnΕ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4483727-n?shelf=favorites-sequential-art">favorites-sequential-art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4483727-n?shelf=favorites-sf-fantasy-horror-crime">favorites-sf-fantasy-horror-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4483727-n?shelf=favorites-artbooks-and-comics">favorites-artbooks-and-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4483727-n?shelf=monograph-japanese-asian-art">monograph-japanese-asian-art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4483727-n?shelf=pb-drkhrse-ksk-lbry-glry-curcol-ed">pb-drkhrse-ksk-lbry-glry-curcol-ed</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1067131857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1613565513272955474"><u>
  <b>Berserk: A Super-Dick Slaughterama the Whole Family Can Enjoy (Except Grandma and Grampa. And the Kids. And Probably the Significant Other. You Might Not Like it Either.)</b>
</u><br/><br/><i>[NOTE: This is really a review of the entire series. Reviewing every single volume sounds like one of those repetitive, mindless exercises used to break down the ego of a subject prior to brainwashing. Explicit and possibly offensive images and language follow, so don't scroll down if that sort of thing makes you feel twitch</i></span>
  <span id="freeText1613565513272955474" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>Berserk: A Super-Dick Slaughterama the Whole Family Can Enjoy (Except Grandma and Grampa. And the Kids. And Probably the Significant Other. You Might Not Like it Either.)</b>
</u><br><br><i>[NOTE: This is really a review of the entire series. Reviewing every single volume sounds like one of those repetitive, mindless exercises used to break down the ego of a subject prior to brainwashing. Explicit and possibly offensive images and language follow, so don't scroll down if that sort of thing makes you feel twitchy and weird... particularly if you own a semi-auto crossbow.]</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449545966ra/17302262.gif" width="400" height="295" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Berserk! If I had of discovered this shit when I was a teenager, I probably would've suffered a fatal wargasm. Dark Age mercenaries with massive fucking swords cutting their enemies into bloody quivering chunks on the field of battle! Sorcerers and demonic knights and characters who aren't all that interested in right and wrong! Huge, anatomically incorrect tits!... and the breasts look a bit off on the female characters too... <br><br><i>Oh yeah! Badly drawn manga-tits! Miura overdoes everything in the first couple volumes, and stylized anatomical distortions are all part of the manga package:</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449545966i/17302263._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="592" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><u>
  <b>Guts:_____________A Tit-pixie stole my nipples. <br>_____________________I'm hideous.<br>_________________Can I borrow one of yours?<br><br>Casca: They're kind of attached. <br>___Maybe yours will grow back.</b>
</u><br><br>Alright, I've used up my monthly GR allotment of exclamation marks. Most series get better as they go on, but the truly epic length of Berserk, now over 37 volumes and counting, has yielded a huge leap in artistry. The quality of the art in the second half of the series is light years ahead of the relatively crude renderings of volume 1, and there's been a gradual refinement to Miura's storytelling that comes with maturity, greater complexity and restraint, letting the tension build, much sharper character development and pacing. <br><br><i>Look at that texturing. The choice between this level of beautiful intricacy and computer coloring ain't no choice at all:</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449545966i/17302265._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="288" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449545966i/17302266._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="285" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That doesn't mean that volume 1 is terrible, by any means; it's just not on the same level as Miura's later work, which rapidly evolves to some of the most elaborate, jaw-droppingly gorgeous work in the medium. The European influence of artists like Francois Schuiten, Hermann and Moebius is evident from the beginning; but it's particularly clear in the beautifully rendered battlefield sequences of volumes 34 to 36, in which the Band of the Hawk's war against the god-like Emperor culminates with a stunning transformation, as Griffin's troops reveal their true demonic selves. The imaginative firepower is very impressive and visually distinctive, with Miura's clean outlines and controlled hatching making every page a work that could stand alone on it's visual merits.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449545966i/17302267._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="297" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449545966i/17302268._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="283" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Taking place in a peculiarly Japanese vision of Medieval Europe, Berserk is a relic of the Dungeons and Dragons-style fantasy boom of the 1980's. It always manages to make me nostalgic for something I never knew, in the same way the film Akira makes me nostalgic for 80's science fiction and cell animation. Berserk attracted a huge fan following immediately, and has since become an international multi-media hit, thanks to the anime and the Dark Horse translation of the manga. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449545966i/17302269._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="297" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The sex-and-violence factor has contributed to its popularity, as Guts, the Black Swordsman, goes 'berserk' and kills everything that breathes, bi-secting his enemies with an eight-inch wide, six-foot long broadsword that is obviously and ridiculously phallic. While swords can always have phallic associations, it seems like Miura has to be conscious of the exaggerated super-dick fantasy he's illustrating every time Guts splits another enemy in two. Then there's the weird, almost-gay rivalry/bromance between Guts and Griffin, the oddly effeminate demon-warlord with a platinum mullet... but that has nothing to do with the early volumes. Or, you know, anything.<br><br><i>The only thing more obviously phallic is a dick. Guts might as well be swinging around a six-foot long dildo:</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449580251i/17308525._SY540_.png" width="400" height="605" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449545966i/17302270._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="616" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449545966ra/17302271.gif" width="400" height="166" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Each volume of Berserk goes by ridiculously fast considering the amount of effort it represents, with the cinematic pacing that is so different from European and American comics. This means that the 'time-lapse' between the panels is much shorter, resulting in more work for the artist. A story that takes 48 pages to tell in a European comic album will take 200 pages as a manga 'tankobon'. In Vagabond, for example, over 120 pages are devoted to a duel; specifically, the seconds spent <i>waiting for the other man to launch his attack</i>. 120 pages detailing the silent, psychic battle that is waged between two indomitable wills. Fear and uncertainty are created or indicated by the slight shift of a sandal. That's not exactly <i>typical</i>, and as much as I like 'Vagabond', I have to admit, that shit got tedious; but it's also far from unprecedented or unique in the manga canon.<br><br><i>Miura adds a homage to Bosch in one of the more recent volumes; he's unquestionably one of the best manga artists alive, on par with Otomo, Satoshi Kon (RIP), and Taiyo Matsumoto. He wasn't this good in the early going, but he developed quickly:</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449545966i/17302272._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="298" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449545966i/17302273._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="292" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Berserk eschews the brand of pretentious, 'overblown subtlety' (an oxymoron that somehow fits in this case) that can make some series feel like 200 pages of writer's block translated as an action sequence, but you still end up going through each volume pretty fast. I deliberately slow things down to enjoy the carefully crafted artwork, but unfortunately, manga does not encourage art scrutiny. I'd like to see Berserk and Blade of the Immortal collected in the larger-sized omnibus editions like 'Viz-Big', which collect three books together, use a better grade of paper, and provide a bigger page to show off the art. They're also far more economical.*<br><br>*P.S.: Thankfully, Dark Horse exceeded my hopes, publishing the entire series (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42120580.Berserk_Deluxe_Edition_Volume_1" title="Berserk Deluxe Edition Volume 1 by Kentaro Miura" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1538526534l/42120580._SX50_.jpg" alt="Berserk Deluxe Edition Volume 1 by Kentaro Miura" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42454096.Berserk_Deluxe_Edition_Volume_2" title="Berserk Deluxe Edition Volume 2 by Kentaro Miura" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1541353114l/42454096._SX50_.jpg" alt="Berserk Deluxe Edition Volume 2 by Kentaro Miura" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44036458.Berserk_Deluxe_Edition_Volume_3" title="Berserk Deluxe Edition Volume 3 by Kentaro Miura" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1550712693l/44036458._SX50_.jpg" alt="Berserk Deluxe Edition Volume 3 by Kentaro Miura" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>, et cetera, et cetera; they're up to releasing Volume 7 soon, which will include the regular tankobon volumes 19, 20, &amp; 21) in a deluxe 7" x 10" hardcover omnibus format, with a better quality paper stock that allows Miura's intricate hatching &amp; screen-tones to be properly appreciated. It's the nicest package I've seen for a manga series - with the possible exception of the Akira 35th Anniversary Box-Set - and it certainly merits such a publishing honor; it's one of the few series that might compel fans who already own all 40 of the tiny tankobon volumes to spend 50$ per volume - 700$ total - on the eventual 14 omnibus volumes collecting the exact same material. It sounds a little crazy when you frame it like that... but for me, getting a more fitting presentation of Kentaro Miura's artistry is well worth it. <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="1613565513272955474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26989936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10519662286774014898">This review will be my review of the whole series.<br/><br/>I think this is easily the best and most epic manga ever written. The drawing is grimy and it has this very old school 1980's feel even up to this day which i think gives it a little something extra. Pound for pound the most visually stunning and sometimes revolting thing I have ever read. Then there is the depth of the mythology. I think this manga has been running for something like 18 years and the story just gets deeper and deeper. I read all</span>
  <span id="freeText10519662286774014898" style="display:none">This review will be my review of the whole series.<br /><br />I think this is easily the best and most epic manga ever written. The drawing is grimy and it has this very old school 1980's feel even up to this day which i think gives it a little something extra. Pound for pound the most visually stunning and sometimes revolting thing I have ever read. Then there is the depth of the mythology. I think this manga has been running for something like 18 years and the story just gets deeper and deeper. I read all of the volumes available last summer and it was one of the most draining and simultaneously rewarding experieneces of my life. The philosophical battle between Guts and Griffith, freedom vs. tranquility. I have argued since with my friends about this over and over again, btu Griffith is absolutely representative of the anti-christ while Guts represents not a Godly and righteous hero, but a man acting for all humanity and freedom of choice, though he doesn't seem to care about anything but vengeance. I liked this manga so much I'm getting the Brand of the Sacrificed tattooed on my heart. Its gonna be epic. I hope everyone who loves comics will read this series at some point in there life and be as blown away as i was. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10519662286774014898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_236651503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236651503" />
    <a title="Petros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6984857-petros"><img alt="Petros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321523871p2/6984857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/236651503?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petros" href="/user/show/6984857-petros">Petros</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236651503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12127320250798535729">Medieval kingdoms, big swords, frenzied warriors, gore, nude, sex, intrigue, betrayal, demons, a quest for vengeance. Berserk is the encapsulation of the best parts of dark fantasy. You know how nowadays everything gets compared to Dark Souls? Even Dark Souls took heavy inspiration from it, if that is any indication for how well executed it is. <br/><br/>And why wouldn’t it be? If pretty images are all you care about, then you will never be disappointed as the artwork is amongst the best you can find in a</span>
  <span id="freeText12127320250798535729" style="display:none">Medieval kingdoms, big swords, frenzied warriors, gore, nude, sex, intrigue, betrayal, demons, a quest for vengeance. Berserk is the encapsulation of the best parts of dark fantasy. You know how nowadays everything gets compared to Dark Souls? Even Dark Souls took heavy inspiration from it, if that is any indication for how well executed it is. <br /><br />And why wouldn’t it be? If pretty images are all you care about, then you will never be disappointed as the artwork is amongst the best you can find in any manga. And despite changing slightly as years go by, it never becomes lazy and dull, as is the case with any other long-running title. Almost every frame is a painting of fine art, extremely detailed and graphical, taking hours to be drawn with attention to facial expressions, clothing and sceneries. Especially the panoramic views showing huge armies clashing are breath taking. <br /><br />Obviously a big part of the charm is also the graphic depictions of people getting slaughtered in all sorts of disgusting ways, women getting raped, and demons looking like the stuff of feverish nightmares. I grew indifferent to all that over the years, since to the most part they come off as shock factor instead of maturity. It’s time to stop thinking the more fucked up something looks the more deep and thought provoking it is. All that stuff look cool, but they are B grade aesthetics for the less demanding audience. <br /><br />What sets Berserk above a typical gorefest is its focus on the mentality of its characters. The world affects the characters and is affected back by them, becoming a double battlefield, one of external enemies and one of internal fears. The demons are not generic creatures of evil as they are mortals who were taken over by their desires and gave up on humanity in the name of lust and ambition. They were not born evil, they became monsters as a result of living in a cruel world where the strong can do anything they want and the weak are expendable cannon fodder. This is not something your average edgelord schlock can show properly, since over there everyone is born psychotic and acts like a maniac over first world problems. <br /><br />Despite that, it still goes overboard in many cases, since anyone who is positive, cheerful, and believes in the kindness of people always ends up getting raped and murdered in the most humiliating ways. There is no counterforce to all the selfish cynicism and good-hearted people are treated as idiots who deserve to be kicked around for not wanting to be ruthless serial killers. The medieval setting sort of excuses it, but half the times it still comes off as petty for the sake of torture porn. <br /> <br />But you know what? This is a minor issue compared to how it’s being made for three decades and there is no ending in sight. Since the Eclipse event, the only thing I wanted to see is Guts getting his final showdown with Griffith, but chances are I am never going to get it because Miura is busy playing Idolmaster and keeps throwing more shit between them to make sure they will never meet. At this rate the creator will die of old age before completing it. I mean, the pacing was always slow and not focused on plot progression as it was on getting to know the characters or getting prolonged random battles in between. But just like it happens with everything that overstays its welcome, it eventually becomes tiresome. <br /><br />I used to love seeing Guts butchering people with progressively bigger swords, but, falling victim to power creep, the stronger creatures he is facing the less dramatization there is behind the action. The typical soldiers in the early arcs were making it far easier to feel the devastation of war. When they got replaced with beasts and eventually with monsters, there’s nothing there anymore. Guts is killing abominations that have nothing humane and thus nothing relatable about them.<br /><br />The story is also expanding beyond its initial premise to something much greater and multilayered. What began as a simple revenge story of one guy versus another guy, it moves away from Guts’ objective and slowly gets enriched with all sorts of extra themes, such as the intrigue of politics, the concept of faith, the origin of magic, and different dimensions overlapping each other. <br /><br />Which is also an issue, since Guts is still the one defeating most of the enemies while everyone else is low level support. Despite the story expanding to include a dozen other characters and themes, it still has the same one guy doing all the work. While Guts was butchering to pieces anyone standing in his way, it was excused because he was getting the spotlight. Now a dozen other characters get some spotlight and are close to worthless in battle. How can you care about all the extra stuff thrown in there when none of them can stand on their own without Guts constantly jumping it to save them? <br /><br />Not to mention the comic relief; it’s so annoying and only increases in volume as time goes on. When the story began, there were no gag characters in Guts’ team, while now half of the team is there just for making silly jokes. Despite the world getting overrun with horrible monsters, most of the depressing atmosphere of the earlier arcs is gone. Now it’s like a mindless hack and slash Dynasty Warriors videogame, where one guy is cynically killing thousands of faceless monsters before throwing in a few cheesy one-liners. <br /><br />This is why the Eclipse was the peak of the story and everything after it keeps feeling less and less interesting. I didn’t give a shit about Griffith fighting that Hindu king, and the whole thing with the pirates and the mermaids was a seven year filler arc. Why do you think everyone makes fun of everything happening after the Eclipse? Because the anime adaptation was cancer CGI? No, because it didn’t have the same interest as before. <br /><br />I will go as far as say the 90s anime adaptation is the best version of them all. Sure, the budget wasn’t the best, but for the material it covered, it was even better than the manga. <br />-It took out the unnecessary battles with filler monsters <br />-It kept the meaningful character interactions<br />-It removed Skull Knight and his plot armor<br />-It removed Puck and his horrible comic relief<br />-It stopped at the Eclipse, the best part of the whole story <br />-The hand-drawn still images were doing a much better job than the cancer CGI of later adaptations<br /><br />Just watch that one and consider the rest mostly a waste of time and a huge disappointment consisting of terrible CGI and clang sounds.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12127320250798535729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

When I write this review the series has been running for around 27 years.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7878665913605636904">Blood, guts (in more ways than one), and huge swords (not even in the phallic symbol kinda way...okay it probably is). I haven't read a lot of manga, but this was great stuff. <br/><br/>Berserk is manga set in medieval times. It's straight-forward, good guy (who's kind of a dick) in pursuit of bad dudes doing bad things.   <span id="freeText7878665913605636904" style="display:none">Blood, guts (in more ways than one), and huge swords (not even in the phallic symbol kinda way...okay it probably is). I haven't read a lot of manga, but this was great stuff. <br /><br />Berserk is manga set in medieval times. It's straight-forward, good guy (who's kind of a dick) in pursuit of bad dudes doing bad things. It has it's mysterious elements that I'm interested in getting to know, but it's really all about taking people out...including slicing horses in half...and the dude has a crazy crossbow that shoots like 10 at once.<br /><br />Not much more to say. I blazed through it in about half an hour and my appetite is only just whetted. <br /><br />Thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4034296-bastard" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bastard </a> for the rec.</span>

<div id="review_869782308" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/869782308" />
    <a title="John Wiswell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/147818-john-wiswell"><img alt="John Wiswell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442531848p2/147818.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/869782308?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Wiswell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Wiswell" href="/user/show/147818-john-wiswell">John Wiswell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer869782308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2170786522764489090">A messy little manga that feels like a graphic artist venting his Dungeons & Dragons empowerment fantasies. Here we follow Guts, the frowny badass with a giant sword, who kills a bunch of bad guys, gets caught and tortured for a little while, then breaks free and kills more bad guys. He goes on a trip and is jumped by skeletons, who he beats up, while frowning. He gets a fairy sidekick, who he frowns at. He’s in pursuit of more bad guys, for reasons we don’t know, but for obvious motives: he’s g</span>
  <span id="freeText2170786522764489090" style="display:none">A messy little manga that feels like a graphic artist venting his Dungeons &amp; Dragons empowerment fantasies. Here we follow Guts, the frowny badass with a giant sword, who kills a bunch of bad guys, gets caught and tortured for a little while, then breaks free and kills more bad guys. He goes on a trip and is jumped by skeletons, who he beats up, while frowning. He gets a fairy sidekick, who he frowns at. He’s in pursuit of more bad guys, for reasons we don’t know, but for obvious motives: he’s going to beat them up. It’s what this volume suggests he exists to do. From adaptations of the series, one knows there must be more to it, but this volume doesn’t have anything more to offer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2170786522764489090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review869782308">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_2822369403" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2822369403" />
    <a title="Juho Pohjalainen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/85347537-juho-pohjalainen"><img alt="Juho Pohjalainen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555446239p2/85347537.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2822369403?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juho Pohjalainen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juho Pohjalainen" href="/user/show/85347537-juho-pohjalainen">Juho Pohjalainen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2822369403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14335347118115742493">Some of the finest fantasy I've ever read and possibly my favourite ongoing story, Berserk nonetheless has a bit of a humble start. Its artwork is still pretty rough and unrefined and not particularly appealing - especially in the case of Puck - and the writing's still pretty shallow and has a fair few inconsistencies overall. Guts himself is just a dark edgy badass that plows his way through small armies and big demons, a character archetype that we've seen a million times since and that rarely</span>
  <span id="freeText14335347118115742493" style="display:none">Some of the finest fantasy I've ever read and possibly my favourite ongoing story, Berserk nonetheless has a bit of a humble start. Its artwork is still pretty rough and unrefined and not particularly appealing - especially in the case of Puck - and the writing's still pretty shallow and has a fair few inconsistencies overall. Guts himself is just a dark edgy badass that plows his way through small armies and big demons, a character archetype that we've seen a million times since and that rarely has anything to offer. The rest of the characters are all basically one-shots who serve for their part in the story and then disappear (usually in pieces) so there's not much to them either.<br /><br />Still, there's a few high points to be had. Fights are already gory and visceral and well-told, the cannon surprise is great, you've got a good bit of skeleton war, a couple quick clues of Guts's character being fleshed out later - a spot of conscience and his hatred of being touched - and the opening scene is hilariously over-the-top even if it contradicts everything we'll learn in the future. If you like this sort of a thing you'll have a good time, provided Puck doesn't annoy you too much.<br /><br />If this is your first entrance to the world of Berserk and you (somehow) know nothing of it, go into it completely blind, this first volume might not be enough to sell you for the long tale to come. But rest assured, it will get better: every criticism I've laid to this - artwork, story, Guts himself, other characters, <i>everything</i> - will be fixed, quite soon at that. If you make it to the end but still have your doubts, let me assuage you and wholeheartedly encourage you to keep on going. You won't regret it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14335347118115742493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1688906698" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11546484078897825761">With the release this summer of the newest Berserk anime, I decided it was time to revisit the Manga. <br/><br/>It's fun going back to the earlier Berserk stories. I forgot how different the original source material really is from the anime(s) they have made/are making.<br/><br/>The Manga is a lot more intense, it's more graphic and doesn't really worry about pulling punches.   <span id="freeText11546484078897825761" style="display:none">With the release this summer of the newest Berserk anime, I decided it was time to revisit the Manga. <br /><br />It's fun going back to the earlier Berserk stories. I forgot how different the original source material really is from the anime(s) they have made/are making.<br /><br />The Manga is a lot more intense, it's more graphic and doesn't really worry about pulling punches. Hell, the very first panel, Guts is banging a demon slut...and it only gets <s>worse</s> better from there.<br /><br />The art in this series is top notch and suits the dark and grimy atmosphere of the world well. The entire volume is jam packed full of action and giant swords...or...well...full of action and one giant sword at least.<br /><br />The Berserk story is a pretty epic one and this first volume doesn't even scratch the surface of where things eventually go - but it's still a fun volume full of violence and carnage.<br /><br />Everything a Berserk fan needs, really.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10607575998849774415">Berserk doesn't hold back in terms of violence and gore, but unlike many other books in the format, it doesn't have violence just for the sake of violence. The art isn't gorgeous to look at, but it is good enough and blends well with the setting of the manga. So, if you're looking for a violent dark fantasy manga, then Berserk is just for you.</span>

<div id="review_1304291542" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1304291542" />
    <a title="Michael Sorbello" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4307906-michael-sorbello"><img alt="Michael Sorbello" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521124600p2/4307906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1304291542?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Sorbello" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Sorbello" href="/user/show/4307906-michael-sorbello">Michael Sorbello</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4307906-michael-sorbello?shelf=all-comics">all-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4307906-michael-sorbello?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4307906-michael-sorbello?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1304291542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14245903180518679765">Hellraiser + Conan the Barbarian + Game of Thrones + Ash vs Evil Dead + Macbeth = Berserk.<br/><br/>There's a joke in the Berserk community that no matter how bad you have it, Guts will always have it worse. It's not all that hard to believe once you've delved into the psychologically devastating slaughter fest that is Berserk.<br/><br/>Guts was born from the corpse of a dead woman hanging from a tree and adopted into a group of brutal mercenaries as a baby. He watched the closest thing he had to a real mother die </span>
  <span id="freeText14245903180518679765" style="display:none">Hellraiser + Conan the Barbarian + Game of Thrones + Ash vs Evil Dead + Macbeth = Berserk.<br /><br />There's a joke in the Berserk community that no matter how bad you have it, Guts will always have it worse. It's not all that hard to believe once you've delved into the psychologically devastating slaughter fest that is Berserk.<br /><br />Guts was born from the corpse of a dead woman hanging from a tree and adopted into a group of brutal mercenaries as a baby. He watched the closest thing he had to a real mother die from the plague. He was violently abused by his adoptive father and sold to a rapist as a small child. He was forced to kill his parent. He watched all of his friends and loved ones get tortured, raped and eaten alive right in front of him. He was betrayed and marked as a demonic sacrifice by the man he considered his closest friend. And that's only the beginning.<br /><br />Berserk has always been my favorite manga of all time, rivalled only by Naoki Urasawa's Monster. The first volume is only the tip of the iceberg of a very complex, dark and violent tragedy. If you find yourself to be not too impressed with the first volume, I highly recommend reading further. The first three volumes serve as an interlude to help prepare you for the atrocities to come and may seem somewhat underwhelming in terms of plot, but believe me when I say the payoff is highly rewarding and memorable.<br /><br />Guts seems like a simplistic, edgy anti-hero at first glance, but he's so much more than that. Guts is one of the greatest characters the fantasy genre has to offer, Sigmund Freud could probably write a novel-length psychological analysis of the severely troubled and broken man. Not to mention his rival Griffith who is equally complex and incredibly rich with psychological depth, but there will be more on that as you delve further in. I would strongly recommend this series for hardcore fans of fantasy and horror, so long as you're prepared to be traumatized for life by the disgustingly harsh nature of its content.<br /><br />***<br /><br />My Social Media<br /><br />My Instagram Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/michael_sorbello/">https://www.instagram.com/michael_sor...</a><br /><br />My Wattpad Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.wattpad.com/user/Michael-Sorbello">https://www.wattpad.com/user/Michael-...</a><br /><br />My YouTube Channel: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCPPs1eOzsOqcz5ey5JjGSbg">https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCPPs...</a><br /><br />My Twitter Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/SorbelloHorror">https://twitter.com/SorbelloHorror</a><br /><br />My Facebook Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/michael.sorbello.104">https://www.facebook.com/michael.sorb...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14245903180518679765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11150280545060473331">Ah, Berserk: manga that dwarfs all other manga. Not all volumes of this neverending dark fantasy saga are equally gripping, but most of those covering the Golden Age arc are really outstanding, and when Miura is in top form he is unbeatable, much like his brooding anti-hero, the übermensch Guts. <br/><br/>The plot of Berserk is brutal and intricate, full of twists, turns and cliffhangers; the action is merciless, violent and gruesome; but the characters and their interactions are the crux that makes the s</span>
  <span id="freeText11150280545060473331" style="display:none">Ah, Berserk: manga that dwarfs all other manga. Not all volumes of this neverending dark fantasy saga are equally gripping, but most of those covering the Golden Age arc are really outstanding, and when Miura is in top form he is unbeatable, much like his brooding anti-hero, the übermensch Guts. <br /><br />The plot of Berserk is brutal and intricate, full of twists, turns and cliffhangers; the action is merciless, violent and gruesome; but the characters and their interactions are the crux that makes the story truly shine. Also, the love/hate relationship between Guts and his best friend/arch-nemesis Griffith is the stuff of legends: a tragedy of epic proportions, full of tenderness, devotion, angst, betrayal and pain, with enough unresolved sexual tension to inflame the passions of a thousand nuns. <br /><br />Anyways, this first volume is only so-so--great stuff is yet to come. But on the whole (or at least counting volumes 3-13, which I think are the best ones), this manga is up there among my favorite reads of all time, and I highly recommend it. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="bookjunkie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="bookjunkie" href="/user/show/52486272-bookjunkie">bookjunkie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1884486075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13010978546000065638">***This is a review of the whole series***<br/><br/>Berserk is not for the squeamish. I tried to read a volume while eating once. I did not make that mistake again.<br/><br/>Dark fantasy apparently contains a subgenre called <i>grimdark</i>. It is what it sounds like: fantasy with a particularly grim and dark atmosphere, permeated with horror and dread. This accurately describes Berserk's gritty, violent, fantasy-medieval setting, but it is also realistic. I mean, humans created torture. Judas cradles, the rack, the wheel</span>
  <span id="freeText13010978546000065638" style="display:none">***This is a review of the whole series***<br><br>Berserk is not for the squeamish. I tried to read a volume while eating once. I did not make that mistake again.<br><br>Dark fantasy apparently contains a subgenre called <i>grimdark</i>. It is what it sounds like: fantasy with a particularly grim and dark atmosphere, permeated with horror and dread. This accurately describes Berserk's gritty, violent, fantasy-medieval setting, but it is also realistic. I mean, humans created torture. Judas cradles, the rack, the wheel: these were all actual medieval torture devices. Humans also are responsible for hatred, brutality, lust, and war. Miura did not make up any of these things, he merely depicts them in all their awful, sobering reality.<br><br>I'm not a horror fan. In fact, I hate it. I don't watch Saw movies, or any other type of movie with gratuitous gore. I mistakenly watched Silent Hill at a sleepover once and wanted to burn my eyes out, felt sick the entire night. I actually tend towards cheesy, happy, uplifting movies. Disney, Pixar, August Rush, Billy Elliot, those are really much more my kind of thing. However, there's something to be said for movies that mix light with darkness. <i>Life Is Beautiful</i>, for example, is a movie that made a deep impression on me. A father creates a grand game of Let's-Pretend for his young son when they're placed in a concentration camp. Throughout their whole imprisonment, the son never realizes the reality of their nightmarish situation because of his father's protection and sacrifice. The love and hope shining through in that movie hit me harder <i>because</i> of the bleakness, cruelty, and death surrounding them.<br><br>You won't find much love and hope in Berserk. It's full of ugliness and evil, and there's no love to counteract that. There <i>is</i>, however, a defiant refusal to bow to fate. You might say it's the human spirit of perseverance. You know that scene in Game of Thrones where a massive army mounted on horses is thundering down upon a single man standing on foot alone in a battlefield, and the man's reaction upon seeing his fast-approaching certain death is to draw his sword? That single majestic scene sums up the essence of Berserk. Berserk is an epic story of a lone man struggling against overwhelming, <i>impossible</i> odds, rebelling against the literal hand of fate. <br><br>Miura began this series in 1989, and his early work is a bit clumsy. At first, the artwork is awkward, almost cutesy. The dialogue is heavy-handed and cliche, the action is comic-book generic. In fact, the story itself doesn't seem like anything special until the Golden Age Arc, around Volume 4. If you manage to plod your way through to that point, however, you'll be in for an insane ride. Somehow, with each successive volume, the story only becomes more and more epic, until around Volume 30 you'll have experienced all the heights and depths fantasy has to offer, from knights to monsters, peaceful villagers to marauding raiders. From witches and elves and fairies, to demons and trolls and literal <i>Gods</i>. The artwork, too, becomes increasingly intricate, lush, and mind-blowingly beautiful.<br><br>The story boils down to this: Guts is destined to be a loser. He's a loser from the moment he's born, slipping out of his dead mother who's hanging from a tree into a pile of her guts. He's a loser when the mercenary who raises him pimps him out to be raped as a child. He loses his best friend when he strikes out for independence, he loses his true love when his best friend betrays them all for god-hood and rapes Guts's lover into madness. He loses his arm, and he loses his eye. He loses all his friends and companions. He even loses his unborn child to demonic corruption. He loses his chance at peace and a future when he's marked by a demon brand, labeling him as demon-food, attracting unholy creatures and the undead every night to try and feast on him. There can be no character ever imagined in the history of fiction quite as incredibly, relentlessly, mercilessly unfortunate as Guts. Not only are the living and dead both against him, but the gods themselves want to crush him.<br><br>Guts's answer to all this?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484782086i/21753119._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>He draws his fucking sword.</i><br><br>Guts doesn't know how to roll over and die. He's not programmed to accept his fate. He's missing the logic chip that tells the rest of us when to give up, when something has a foregone conclusion. He's not particularly intelligent; he's not kind, or sensitive, or philosophical. He's a big dumb brute with a gift for fighting who unhesitatingly pits himself against omnipotent evil, uncaring of how alone he is in his stand, uncaring of how impossible it is for him to win.<br><br>There are a few very different story arcs in this series, all equally fascinating. It's still ongoing (almost thirty years...) but I'm happy to note that somehow, the tone has gotten brighter near the later volumes. Guts, utterly alone for so long, has found himself some companions. An adorably timid yet immensely powerful witch-girl, a sneaky, trouble-making little urchin kid, two pixie-like elves, a troubled noblewoman and her faithful manservant. This fellowship brings some warmth and humanity back to Guts, and the heavy darkness of the continuing storyline somehow seems to hang lighter. Makes me wonder if Miura hasn't perhaps worked out some personal demons as the series progressed, and now he's in a better place. <br><br>I've spent a lot of money collecting this series, and even as I move all the rest of my books to digital copies, my Berserk collection will stay on its treasured shelf of honor. Once the series is finally completed, I have no doubt it will be one of the most epic stories ever told.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13010978546000065638" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1600391459512301092">Kentaro Miura is one of my favourite artists.   <span id="freeText1600391459512301092" style="display:none">Kentaro Miura is one of my favourite artists. His illustrations are so detailed and amazing, the character designs are stylized, unique and well done that they tell us a lot about the personalities even without the narration and dialogue, and the action sequences are especially so well drawn. The art just becomes better and better as the manga progresses. The dark and gruesome nature of the art also matches the story perfectly well.<br /><br />The story starts with the Black swordsman called Guts hunting some demons known as the Apostles. He also meets his Elf sidekick "puck" in the first chapter. As the story progresses we keep learning more about the world that Berserk is set in and the past of our protagonist and the motives that are driving him. The way his past is unraveled and the story progresses is just brilliant storytelling.<br />Not just the character design but the character development and their progression as the characters evolve is also handled really well.<br /><br />On the whole Berserk is a great fantasy action manga with an intricate plot, believable and well written characters and some of the best illustrated action sequences. There is plenty of action, violence and blood and gore.</span>

  <span id="freeText11153925519267929573" style="display:none">Wow, that was violent! A little too violent for me, but I thought it was well drawn and there was lots of comic relief with the little elf, Puck.<br /><br />This is the story of a man with a brand. <span id="freeTextContainer7470021459983478411">3.5 stars maybe?<br/><br/>I'm surprised by how much I liked this volume. I don't usually read middle-age-esque fantasy manga with lots of fighting & gore & violence.<br/><br/>Guts is on a quest to kill demons and other despicable creatures, however he's not the knight in shining armor, he couldn't care less about casualties and innocent people killed in the process.   <span id="freeText7470021459983478411" style="display:none">3.5 stars maybe?<br /><br />I'm surprised by how much I liked this volume. I don't usually read middle-age-esque fantasy manga with lots of fighting &amp; gore &amp; violence.<br /><br />Guts is on a quest to kill demons and other despicable creatures, however he's not the knight in shining armor, he couldn't care less about casualties and innocent people killed in the process. He believes if a person is too weak to defend themselves they deserves what's coming for them. I'm curious to see where his arc will go.<br /><br />I love Puck, they're an elf and they are as shook with Guts ruthlessness as I am.<br /><br />This volume was originally published in 1990 and it's the oldest manga I've read as of today. The artwork is not something I would've typically enjoy but it works for this story.<br /><br />To sum up, I was going into this manga being 80% sure I wouldn't like it but I've liked it enough to continue on with the series. I want to see what happens next.<br /><br /><u>CW:</u> gore, violence, graphic depiction of them</span>

<div id="review_257781284" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/257781284" />
    <a title="Yasiru" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6226405-yasiru"><img alt="Yasiru" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328436433p2/6226405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/257781284?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yasiru" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yasiru" href="/user/show/6226405-yasiru">Yasiru</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6226405-yasiru?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6226405-yasiru?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6226405-yasiru?shelf=to-purchase">to-purchase</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257781284" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8964556563657351273">Being a review of the entire (yet ongoing) series.<br/><br/>It is a rare thing that a work can abstract what aspects of the human condition it explores to a raw essence of struggle instead of merely accomplishing a transference of symptoms from our familiar world to a more tightly controlled, constructed realm, as do most works of fantasy. Indeed, it's easy for the more human themes to become subsumed quite colourlessly into an endeavour of vivid world-building.<br/><br/>The world of Berserk makes no such compromis</span>
  <span id="freeText8964556563657351273" style="display:none">Being a review of the entire (yet ongoing) series.<br /><br />It is a rare thing that a work can abstract what aspects of the human condition it explores to a raw essence of struggle instead of merely accomplishing a transference of symptoms from our familiar world to a more tightly controlled, constructed realm, as do most works of fantasy. Indeed, it's easy for the more human themes to become subsumed quite colourlessly into an endeavour of vivid world-building.<br /><br />The world of Berserk makes no such compromises. It reveals itself, in the slow and steady manner (quite apart from Miura's inconsistent release schedule) of wine taking flavour with age, to be second to none in detail, drawing mainly on early pagan beliefs of magic and an exceedingly authentic medieval feel to both battle and the more mundane things; and yet, never does the series give in to the temptation of letting the world determine the story's course. Instead, the story is moved by the aforementioned essential struggle of existence, of man's defiance, ever choked and thwarted by the overwhelming tide of the inevitable. This theme of man's struggle against causality is the defining characteristic of Berserk, embodied by its protagonist Gutts, and its subtlety is what makes it so all-pervading. Never indulging human propensity for self-flattery or underlying benevolence in the world or its machinations, hopes of Gutts (already suffering rejection and guilt as we come to the story) making it out triumphant, unscathed and whole are soon dashed. The weight on him, and the twisting of his own mind, becomes closer and closer to unbearable. As Nietzsche once said, "Battle not with monsters, lest ye become a monster, and if you gaze into the abyss, the abyss gazes also into you."<br /><br />In bringing the story to a head, Miura demonstrates a mastery of storytelling that is impressive regardless of form or genre. Ambition is the central theme that drives the first part of the story (and political machinations follow war efforts), and what it is to be caught in the swirl of a charismatic other's impossible dreams and what it is to belong. The twisting of this ambition and its vessel into a base force when all seems lost, and the insatiable need for vengeance upon destiny's favoured for betrayed dreams, not of your own, but of those you belong with, provides for Gutts, with traumatic abruptness, the purpose without which he broods for the longest time. Where the supernatural is invoked, the significance is cleverly overlaid early on with those darker tones of the series that make it unpalatable to some (and also 'raw' in the sense from earlier).<br /><br />The artwork is nothing short of breathtaking for its detail, and continually improves over the course of the series. This first volume is something of a displaced snapshot of the future, and serves to establish the foreboding, inevitable tone the series manages so well. It is not, however, typical of the style or flow to come later. The releases are irregular and rare, but the series retains a strong following exactly because of its incredible storytelling. An anime series covering the first arc has been around a while now, while a new series is planned for the rest of the series and animated films are due for release covering the same ground as the original series. It can be hoped that this brings back some regularity to the manga releases, but whatever the case, you will be better for having read this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8964556563657351273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Manaf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5326093-manaf"><img alt="Manaf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303928005p2/5326093.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/489381116?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manaf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manaf" href="/user/show/5326093-manaf">Manaf</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer489381116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15685253143777940467">This is one of the most violent manga I have ever seen. While it is extremely dark and twisted, you are going to love how the author builds up this story and how the main character develops from one plot point to another.<br/><br/>The story kicks off with Gatts the black swordsman, who wander the country aimlessly to kill demons. Later on, the plot goes back to Gatts childhood and how did he grow up to become what he is.<br/><br/>I consider this manga one of my all time favourite but I cannot give it full stars. I </span>
  <span id="freeText15685253143777940467" style="display:none">This is one of the most violent manga I have ever seen. While it is extremely dark and twisted, you are going to love how the author builds up this story and how the main character develops from one plot point to another.<br /><br />The story kicks off with Gatts the black swordsman, who wander the country aimlessly to kill demons. Later on, the plot goes back to Gatts childhood and how did he grow up to become what he is.<br /><br />I consider this manga one of my all time favourite but I cannot give it full stars. I think the first chapters took too long and the reader was left in the dark to wonder "what on earth is going on?!". Also the author takes too much time to produce a chapter and people often leave Berserk for a year because they cannot read chapter per month!<br /><br />If you want to read this, you have to be adult and you are prepared to see all kind of ugliness of our world. There are also 3 movies on the first hundred chapters of Berserk. Hopefully the movies will bring life in the manga and the author will finally pick up the pace and finish what he has started in 1990.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BPZizFiuC/nmtNRSpDNLuJewrUBboHiP9UrOAqzbMz1rIGS8+JMlLCCLUEteY4oNF0RQXF4P9N0F2+cApYnuRg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/145435.Kentaro_Miura">About Kentaro Miura</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/145435.Kentaro_Miura"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1275384473p3/145435.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/145435.Kentaro_Miura">Kentaro Miura
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
979
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4329843251347220559">Kentarou Miura (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7418603._' rel='nofollow noopener'>三浦 建太郎</a>) was born in Chiba City, Chiba Prefecture, Japan, in 1966. He is left-handed. In 1976, at the early age of 10, Miura made his first Manga, entitled "Miuranger", that was published for his classmates in a school publication; the manga ended up spanning 40 volumes. In 1977, Miura created his second manga called Ken e no michi (剣への道 The Way to the Sword), using Indian ink for t</span>
  <span id="freeText4329843251347220559" style="display:none">Kentarou Miura (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7418603._" rel="nofollow noopener">三浦 建太郎</a>) was born in Chiba City, Chiba Prefecture, Japan, in 1966. He is left-handed. In 1976, at the early age of 10, Miura made his first Manga, entitled "Miuranger", that was published for his classmates in a school publication; the manga ended up spanning 40 volumes. In 1977, Miura created his second manga called Ken e no michi (剣への道 The Way to the Sword), using Indian ink for the first time. When he was in middle school in 1979, Miura's drawing techniques improved greatly as he started using professional drawing techniques. His first dōjinshi was published, with the help of friends, in a magazine in 1982.<br /><br />That same year, in 1982, Miura enrolled in an artistic curriculum in high school, where he and his classmates started publishing their works in school booklets, as well as having his first dōjinshi published in a fan-produced magazine. In 1985, Miura applied for the entrance examination of an art college in Nihon University. He submitted Futanabi for examination and was granted admission. This project was later nominated Best New Author work in Weekly Shōnen Magazine. Another Miura manga Noa was published in Weekly Shōnen Magazine the very same year. Due to a disagreement with one of the editors, the manga was stalled and eventually dropped altogether. This is approximately where Miura's career hit a slump.<br /><br />In 1988, Miura bounced back with a 48-page manga known as Berserk Prototype, as an introduction to the current Berserk fantasy world. It went on to win Miura a prize from the Comi Manga School. In 1989, after receiving a doctorate degree, Kentarou started a project titled King of Wolves (王狼, ōrō?) based on a script by Buronson, writer of Hokuto no Ken. It was published in the monthly Japanese Animal House magazine in issues 5 and 7 of that year.<br /><br />In 1990, a sequel is made to Ourou entitled Ourou Den (王狼伝 ōrō den, The Legend of the Wolf King) that was published as a prequel to the original in Young Animal Magazine. In the same year, the 10th issue of Animal House witnesses the first volume of the solo project Berserk was released with a relatively limited success. Miura again collaborated with Buronson on manga titled Japan, that was published in Young Animal House from the 1st issue to the 8th of 1992, and was later released as a stand-alone tankōbon. Miura's fame grew after Berserk was serialized in Young Animal in 1992 with the release of "The Golden Age" story arc and the huge success of his masterpiece made of him one of the most prominent contemporary mangakas. At this time Miura dedicates himself solely to be working on Berserk. He has indicated, however, that he intends to publish more manga in the future.<br /><br />In 1997, Miura supervised the production of 25 anime episodes of Berserk that aired in the same year on NTV. Various art books and supplemental materials by Miura based on Berserk are also released. In 1999, Miura made minor contributions to the Dreamcast video game Sword of the Berserk: Guts' Rage. 2004 saw the release of yet another video game adaptation entitled Berserk Millennium Falcon Arc: Chapter of the Record of the Holy Demon War.<br /><br />Since that time, the Berserk manga has spanned 34 tankōbon with no end in sight. The series has also spawned a whole host of merchandise, both official and fan-made, ranging from statues, action figures to key rings, video games, and a trading card game. In 2002, Kentarou Miura received the second place in the Osamu Tezuka Culture Award of Excellence for Berserk.[1]<br /><br />Miura provided the design for the Vocaloid Kamui Gakupo, whose voice is taken from the Japanese singer and actor, Gackt.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4329843251347220559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
